  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_19775812-21b1-44a5-aadc-64ec97c62a15'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17889050099882373523">Gipsy’s Acre was a truly beautiful upland site with views out to sea – and in Michael Rogers it stirred a child-like fantasy. There, amongst the dark fir trees, he planned to build a house, find a girl and live happily ever after. Yet, as he left the village, a shadow of menace hung over the land. For this was the place where accidents happened. Perhaps Michael should have</span>
  <span id="freeText17889050099882373523" style="display:none">Gipsy’s Acre was a truly beautiful upland site with views out to sea – and in Michael Rogers it stirred a child-like fantasy. There, amongst the dark fir trees, he planned to build a house, find a girl and live happily ever after. Yet, as he left the village, a shadow of menace hung over the land. For this was the place where accidents happened. Perhaps Michael should have heeded the locals’ warnings: ‘There’s no luck for them as meddles with Gipsy’s Acre.’ Michael Rogers is a man who is about to learn the true meaning of the old saying ‘In my end is my beginning.’<br /><br />The title Endless Night was taken from William Blake’s Auguries of Innocence and describes Christie’s favourite theme in the novel: a “twisted” character, who always chooses evil over good.<br /><br />Christie finished Endless Night in six weeks, as opposed to the three-four months that most of her other novels took. Despite being in her seventies while writing it, she told an interviewer that being Michael, the twenty-something narrator, “wasn’t difficult. After all, you hear people like him talking all the time.”<br /><br />The book is dedicated to Christie's relative "Nora Prichard from whom I first heard the legend of Gipsy's Acre." Gipsy's Acre was a field on the Welsh moors.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17889050099882373523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

    <div id=buyButtonContainer class="uitext buttons buyableFeature u-marginTopXSmall u-paddingBottomXSmall u-bottomGrayBorder" data-book-id=16366 >

    <div class="u-positionRelative">

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I think he was a person who like Mike had done bad things in the past but was trying to not do them now and to do something good. he found his "salvat<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I think he was a person who like Mike had done bad things in the past but was trying to not do them now and to do something good. he found his "salvation" in his architecture and I think he saw that darkness in Mike and hoped that Mike could change. I don't think he knew he was a murderer but I think he saw something was wrong with him. I think the character was used also as the conscious that Mike didn't have and his death represented Mike losing finally any bit of consciousness he had. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63137841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16110270601005460236"><b>Endless Night, Agatha Christie</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Every night and every morn, Some to misery are born, Every morn and every night, Some are born to sweet delight. Some are born to sweet delight, Some are born to endless night.</i>
</b> WILLIAM BLAKE<br/><br/>The story begins with Michael telling us about his time as a chauffeur and how he met the architect Rudolph Santonix. He plans to one day have a house built by Santonix. <br/><br/>Michael is walking along a village road near the Gipsy's Acre property one day when he meets Ellie, a weal</span>
  <span id="freeText16110270601005460236" style="display:none"><b>Endless Night, Agatha Christie</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Every night and every morn, Some to misery are born, Every morn and every night, Some are born to sweet delight. Some are born to sweet delight, Some are born to endless night.</i>
</b> WILLIAM BLAKE<br /><br />The story begins with Michael telling us about his time as a chauffeur and how he met the architect Rudolph Santonix. He plans to one day have a house built by Santonix. <br /><br />Michael is walking along a village road near the Gipsy's Acre property one day when he meets Ellie, a wealthy heiress who wants to escape from her world of snobby friends, begging relatives, and restrictive financial advisors. As it turns out Ellie had purchased Gipsy's Acre before they met, they decide to marry and build a house at Gipsy's Acre acre with Santonix. <br /><br />The newlywed couple decide to go around the village meeting its residents but are threatened by an old gypsy woman, Mrs Lee, who warns them and instructs them to leave because of a curse.<br /><br />Ellie sustains an injury and invites her companion, Greta Andersen, over to stay with them. Ellie begins to worry about Mike and Greta, as they get into heated arguments. <br /><br />While at lunch with Major Philpot, Mike begins to worry about the fact that Ellie has not yet joined them after going out horse riding. <br /><br />The next day, they find Ellie dead and having sustained no apparent injuries, the local police determine that Ellie died of shock, likely induced when she encountered Mrs Lee. Ellie also had a heart condition. <br /><br />Michael travels to America to attend Ellie’s funeral with her family and collect the inheritance. While there he hears that Mrs Lee has been found dead in a quarry, and Claudia Hardcastle (one of Ellie’s friends from the village) has also died whilst out riding. <br /><br />After Ellie's funeral, Mike goes to visit Santonix on his deathbed. Right before Santonix dies, he screams, “You should have gone the other way!” Feeling disturbed by this, Mike returns to the UK on a sea voyage to give him time to reflect. ...<br /><br />نخستین خوانش: ماه ژانویه سال 2001میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: شب بی پایان؛ نویسنده: آگاتا کریستی (میلر)؛ مترجم: رکسانا یغمائی؛ شیراز، نوید شیراز، 1370؛ در 169ص؛ موضوع داستانهای پلیسی کارآگاهی از نویسندگان انگلیسی - سده 20م<br /><br />عنوان: شب بی پایان؛ نویسنده: آگاتا کریستی (میلر)؛ مترجم: مجتبی عبدالله نژاد؛ تهران، هرمس (کارآگاه)، 1380؛ در 278 ص؛ شابک 9647100485؛ چاپ دوم 1384؛ چاپ سوم 1387؛ شابک 9789647100489؛ چاپ پنجم 1393؛ <br /><br /><b>
  <i>هر شبانگاه و هر سپیده دمان<br />پا گذارند مردمی به جهان<br />که بود سهمشان غم و حرمان<br />هر شبانگاه و هر سپیده دمان<br />پا گذارند مردمی به جهان<br />عده ای را نصیب شادی و شور، عده ای را شبان بی پایان<br />ویلیام بلیک</i>
</b><br /><br />چاپ نخستین از این داستان: «شب بی پایان»، اثر «آگاتا کریستی»، در سال 1967میلادی، و در 224ص، در «کلوب کالینز کرایم» «لندن» بوده است؛ داستان جوانی به نام «مایکل روجرز» را بازگو می‌کند، که با دختر ثروتمندی آشنا شده، و با او ازدواج می‌کند؛ پس از ازدواج، «مایکل» و همسرش، خانه‌ ای متعلق به دوره ی «ویکتوریا» را خریداری می‌کنند؛ خانه‌ ای که به نظر مردمان منطقه، زمین‌های اطرافش «کولی آباد» نام گرفته؛ و نفرین شده است؛ ...؛<br /><br />نقل از آغاز متن: (آغاز من در انجام من است؛ عبارتی است که بارها از زبان مردم شنیده ام؛ درست هم به نظر میرسد؛ ولی راستی به چه معناست؟ <br />آیا نقطه بخصوصی هست که بتوان بر آن انگشت گذاشت و گفت: «ماجرا همه از این روز آغاز شد، از این لحظه بخصوص و در این جای بخصوص و با این حادثه بخصوص؟...»؛ ماجرای من شاید از آنجا آغاز شد که چشمم به آگهی فروش افتاد، که بر دیوار فروشگاه «جورج اَند دراگون»، نصب بود و خبر از فروش مزایده ای ملک قیمتی و ارزشمند «بروج» میداد، و ضمن توصیف جزئیات مساحت آن به میل و فرلانگ، با تصویری کاملاً ایده آل از عمارت «بروج» همراه بود؛ تصویری که شاید مال نخستین سالهای احداث آن در حدود هشتاد تا صد سال پیش بود؛ کار خاصی نداشتم؛ همین طور در خیابان اصلی کینگستون بیشاپ، که دهکده ای است کاملاً بی اهمیت و معمولی، قدم میزدم و وقت تلف میکردم، چشمم به آگهی فروش افتاد؛ چرا؟ دست تقدیر در کار طرح دسیسه ای بود، یا سهم مرا از شادی و خوشبختی به من ارزانی داشت؟ هر طور که خواستید حساب کنید<br /><br />یا شاید بتوان گفت که ماجرا همه از زمانی آغاز شد که «سانتونیکس» را دیدم و با او حرف زدم؛ میتوانم چشمهایم را ببندم و گونه های شاداب و چشمهای براق، و حرکت دستهای قوی، و در عین حال ظریفش را، که نقشه ها و نقشه نماهای خانه ها را رسم میکرد و میکشید، ببینم؛ مخصوصا یکی از آن خانه ها که خانه ای فوق العاده زیبا بود و داشتنش برای من رویایی بود!؛<br /><br />آرزوی داشتن خانه ای، خانه ای زیبا و قشنگ، خانه ای که هرگز امید داشتنش را نداشتم، همان روزها بود که در من بیدار شد؛ رویای شاد و مسرّت آوری مشترک میان ما بود، خانه ای که سانتونیکس برای من میساخت، اگر چندان عمر میکرد؛ خانه ای که در خیالاتم با دختری که دوستش میداشتم در آن زندگی میکردم؛ خانه ای که مثل قهرمانان قصه های پریانِ کودکان، هر دو باید «از آن پس شاد و خوشبخت» در آن زندگی میکردیم؛ همه هم خیالات، همه هم پوچ، ولی بیانگر بیدار شدن آرزویی در من بود...؛ آرزوی داشتن چیزی که هرگز احتمال داشتنش را نداشتم<br /><br />یا اگر این داستانی عشقی است ــ که شک ندارم که هست ــ پس چرا از آنجا آغاز نکنم که چشمم به «اِلی» افتاد، که در پناه درختان صنوبرِ «کولی آباد» ایستاده بود؛ «کولی آباد»، آری؛ شاید بهتر آنست که از همان جا آغاز کنم؛ از لحظه ای که از جلو تابلوی فروش چرخیدم؛ درست همان لحظه ابری سیاه جلو خورشید را گرفته بود، و من کمی احساس سرما و لرز میکردم؛ با کمی بیخیالی از یکی از اهالی محل که به گونه ای سرسری مشغول چیدن علفهای چپری در همان حوالی بود پرسیدم: ــ این خانه هه، «بروج» ، چه جور خانه ای است؟ هنوز چهره متعجب پیرمرد را که از گوشه چشم نگاهم کرد در خاطرم هست؛ گفت: ــ ما بهش نمیگوییم «بروج»، بروج دیگر چه جور اسمی است؟ فینی کرد و ناخشنودیاش را نشان داد و گفت: ــ سالها از زمانیکه کسانی در آن زندگی میکردند و به آن «بروج» میگفتند، میگذرد؛ دوباره فین کرد؛ پرسیدم که پس این خانه را چه مینامند، و او دوباره به آن شیوه ی عجیب و مخصوص دهاتیها، که نخواهند مستقیم و رودررو با تو سخن بگویند، چشمهایش را در صورت پیرِ چروکیده اش، از من چرخاند، و انگار که چیزی ببیند که من نبینم، از بالای شانه یا شاید از گوشه چشم نگاهم کرد و گفت: ــ مردم این حوالی بهش میگویند «کولی آباد»؛ پرسیدم: ــ چرا «کولی آباد»؟ ــ داستانی دارد؛ درست نمیدانم؛ هر کسی چیزی میگوید؛ بعد ادامه داد: ــ به هر حال حوادثی اینجا رخ داده؛ ــ حادثه اتومبیل؟ ــ همه جور حادثه ای؛ این روزها بیشتر حرفِ حادثه اتومبیل است.)»؛ پایان نقل <br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 15/06/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="16110270601005460236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_824788282" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/824788282" />
    <a title="Delee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6168268-delee"><img alt="Delee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552004622p2/6168268.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/824788282?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Delee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Delee" href="/user/show/6168268-delee">Delee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671494537" href="/book/show/7556078-endless-night">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Delee by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira">Ivonne Rovira</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6168268-delee?shelf=mystery-british">mystery-british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6168268-delee?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6168268-delee?shelf=agatha-christie">agatha-christie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6168268-delee?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer824788282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18328279105169362412"><i>In my end is just my beginning...</i><br/><br/>After reading <u>A LOT</u> of Agatha Christie novels in the past, ENDLESS NIGHT- I would have to say- is one of her best, and very different from her others...<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391281549i/8367405.jpg' alt=' photo ad8253b3-eedc-42d0-80c3-0bc49e5f95c2_zpsf8ecd409.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The story is narrated by Michael Rogers- a charming attractive young man- who is a bit of a loner. Michael is unsure about quite a few things in his life, but there are two things he knows for certain. He wants to be rich, and he wants to find a lady and settle down. Out for a walk one day he spots a Sale Bill for</span>
  <span id="freeText18328279105169362412" style="display:none"><i>In my end is just my beginning...</i><br><br>After reading <u>A LOT</u> of Agatha Christie novels in the past, ENDLESS NIGHT- I would have to say- is one of her best, and very different from her others...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391281549i/8367405.jpg" alt=" photo ad8253b3-eedc-42d0-80c3-0bc49e5f95c2_zpsf8ecd409.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story is narrated by Michael Rogers- a charming attractive young man- who is a bit of a loner. Michael is unsure about quite a few things in his life, but there are two things he knows for certain. He wants to be rich, and he wants to find a lady and settle down. Out for a walk one day he spots a Sale Bill for a house being auctioned off nearby -Gipsy Acre- and after exploring the property, he adds another thing to his list. This is where he wants to live. There are a few small problems with his "perfect" plan. The house is in shambles, he has no money, and he has been warned Gipsy Acre is cursed- quite few who have lived there...have also died there. The curse Michael dismisses right away...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391281549i/8367406.jpg" alt=" photo b0309f30-0e8e-46d8-b3db-f0e45e3caf78_zpsdc165320.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The house is also not a problem- Michael's only close friend -Rudolf Santonix- is an architect, and Santonix has always promised that if money, love and property ever became a reality in Michael's life- he would build him the house of his dreams.<br><br>As luck would have it, Michael meets Fenella "Ellie" Guteman- a lovely, wealthy heiress from America- and everything else falls into place. He has the girl, more money than he could have imagined, and as Santonix promised- a breathtaking house on Gipsy Acre. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391281549i/8367407.jpg" alt=" photo ace77ca4-b8a1-4ab9-892d-42d31cdf0bfd_zps4e86f987.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>...but as the lovebirds settle into wedded bliss- strange and frightening things start to happen, and Michael starts to wonder if he will ever get his "happily ever after".<br><br>ENDLESS NIGHT is a eerie little tale, with a splendid twist, and an unsettling conclusion. If you are a Christie fan this is a must read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18328279105169362412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText12804202530049366977" style="display:none">I usually read Agatha Christie to unwind, and although they always guarantee a highly enjoyable hour filled with chuckles and gasps, there is an element of 'lightness' and dismissal involved. <br /><br />Well, that serves me right. This book smacked the patronizing smirk right off my face and I'm drooling on the floor, well and truly humbled. Written lightly, as always, but for the first time, the weight of evil - the kind of evil that wears perfume, goes shopping and is grumpy in the morning - makes its presence softly, sweetly known. <br /><br />Yours truly is humbled, chilled and very impressed. </span>

<div id="review_907468083" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/907468083" />
    <a title="Bionic Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19300421-bionic-jean"><img alt="Bionic Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586709362p2/19300421.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/907468083?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bionic Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bionic Jean" href="/user/show/19300421-bionic-jean">Bionic Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=read-authors-c-d">read-authors-c-d</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=mystery-crime">mystery-crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer907468083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3000516181476245495"><b>Endless Night</b> was one of Agatha Christie's own favourite novels, and one which received the most critical acclaim on its publication in 1967. It is her 58th detective novel. The title is a reference to William Blake's <i>"Auguries of Innocence",<br/><br/>"Every night and every morn,<br/>Some to misery are born,<br/>Every morn and every night,<br/>Some are born to sweet delight.<br/>Some are born to sweet delight,<br/>Some are born to endless night."</i><br/><br/>One of the characters sings and plays this at pertinent points during the book, and i</span>
  <span id="freeText3000516181476245495" style="display:none"><b>Endless Night</b> was one of Agatha Christie's own favourite novels, and one which received the most critical acclaim on its publication in 1967. It is her 58th detective novel. The title is a reference to William Blake's <i>"Auguries of Innocence",<br /><br />"Every night and every morn,<br />Some to misery are born,<br />Every morn and every night,<br />Some are born to sweet delight.<br />Some are born to sweet delight,<br />Some are born to endless night."</i><br /><br />One of the characters sings and plays this at pertinent points during the book, and it becomes evident that it refers to two of the characters. <b>Endless Night</b> has been filmed, adapted as a play and also a graphic novel. It featured in a TV series about Miss Marple (in 2013), although the character of Miss Marple does not appear in the novel. The novels featuring Miss Marple have quite a different feel, so this is an odd inclusion.<br /> <br />Unusually for Agatha Christie, <b>Endless Night</b> has a single viewpoint character, who has a heavy presence in the novel as its narrator. Michael Rogers is a working-class lad whose origins seem to be from a "poor but proud" family with a strong work ethic - which he does not share. He cheerfully admits that he cannot stick to anything. He is unsettled and lazy, having had a variety of jobs. He also appears to the reader to have a chip on his shoulder, and is quite a many-layered character.<br /><br />Very early on in the story, we learn that he has fallen in love with a painting of a house, and has idealised this in his mind to be a "perfect house" which he dreams of owning. He also finds the perfect location for his house in a (fictitious) village called Kington Bishop, near the town of Market Chadwell. In one of his jobs he had worked for an architect, Rudolf Santonix, who has now become a friend. He imagines Santonix designing his perfect dream house, although he knows that acquiring it it is an impossibility. Santonix knows of Michael's strange fantasies and his passion for the imaginary house,<br /><br /><i>"When I was in a fanciful mood I used to think that piece of land had laid a spell upon you. You were a man in love with a house that you might never own, that you might never see, that might never even be built."</i><br /><br />The other main character in the story is almost Michael's complete opposite; a rich American heiress, Funella or "Ellie" Guteman. The two fall in love... but it is as well to remember that this is Agatha Christie, and not her romantic novelist alias "Mary Westmacott", so the course of true love is unlikely to run smooth.<br /><br />This is better written than some of Agatha Christie's novels. The two main characters have far more depth, which the reader learns as the story develops. Sometimes Agatha Christie piles on the characters in order to increase the complexity of the plot, and they inevitably come across as flat stock "types". She will describe their appearance, maybe name their job and a detail or two about their history and feel that she has done enough. She <i>tells </i>us about them. This novel is different, and far better than her average fare, as she <i>reveals</i> Mike and Ellie's characters through their experiences, as told by Mike. <br /><br />Also, to some extent, the characters of Ellie's close companion, Greta Andersen, his mother, the lawyer and guardian "Uncle" Andrew Lippincott, and the terminally-ill architect Rudolf Santonix are more fully fleshed out than usual. But there are secondary characters - the step-mother Cora van Stuyvesant, a friend Claudia Hardcastle, a local bigwig "God" Major Phillpot, the local "witch" Esther Lee and others, who are more akin to Christie's usual cardboard cutouts. <br /><br />The plot itself is satisfying with at least two neat twists near the end, to make the reader gasp. Agatha Christie's strength as a writer is based almost entirely on her ingenious plots. On publication, the newspaper <i>"The Guardian"</i> commented, <i>"the crashing, not to say horrific suspense at the end is perhaps the most devastating that this surpriseful author has ever brought off."</i> And the novelist Robert Barnard calls it, <i>"The best of the late Christies... A splendid late flowering."</i><br /><br />However the literary critic James Zemboy, in his analysis of Agatha Christie's detective novels in 2008, says she was <i>"by then seventy-seven years old and clearly in steep decline as a writer... "Endless Night" is a silly story filled with unlikely events and dull characters... not typical of Agatha Christie... [it is] rather embarrassing."</i><br /><br />Strong words indeed, about quite an enjoyable read. There are deliberate gothic overtones, with the cursed land of "Gipsy's Acre" and the old woman Mrs Lee, with her muttered premonitions of doom. The land is thought to be unlucky, because several accidents have taken place there, particularly on the dangerous curved road approaching the house. <br /><br />The talk of superstitious villagers, resentful gypsies, Mrs Lee, with her dire warnings, who, <i>"Doesn't like the insides of houses. Them as has got gipsy blood don't", </i>the young couple never being happy, the threats against them and <i>"their kind"</i>, the evil site which should never be built on; all these are themes which run throughout the story, unsettling the reader and underpinning the story with a feeling of threat. It is all pure hokum, and the reader feels this is the author's deliberate intention, but it is entertaining and fun.<br /><br /><i>"I'd always known that I'd meet one day a beautiful woman. I had met her. I'd seen her and she'd seen me. We'd come together. A wonderful woman. I'd known the moment I saw her that I belonged to her, belonged to her absolutely and for always. I was hers."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3000516181476245495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2590792019" />
    <a title="Richard Derus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus"><img alt="Richard Derus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494992210p2/3920693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2590792019?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Derus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Derus" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus">Richard Derus</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2590792019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8955874606527622139">I am always sad when I think of this book. Dame Agatha was already in decline due to dementia when, in six short weeks, she flowered this novel. It is the last true Christie novel in the sense that it demonstrates her strengths more clearly than her diminishing powers would ever allow again. That is why I give it four stars.<br/><br/>The story is unremarkable, and in lesser hands would be a tedious oft-told tale. But stop a moment when you feel your eyes start to roll and hold this thought: One of mystery</span>
  <span id="freeText8955874606527622139" style="display:none">I am always sad when I think of this book. Dame Agatha was already in decline due to dementia when, in six short weeks, she flowered this novel. It is the last true Christie novel in the sense that it demonstrates her strengths more clearly than her diminishing powers would ever allow again. That is why I give it four stars.<br /><br />The story is unremarkable, and in lesser hands would be a tedious oft-told tale. But stop a moment when you feel your eyes start to roll and hold this thought: One of mystery fiction's greats (like her work or not, she was indeed a great writer) wrote this, her last lucid writing, before sliding down a slope we all hope we'll never see up close.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.theguardian.com/books/booksblog/2018/nov/06/reading-group-agatha-christie-endless-night-november-book?utm_term=RWRpdG9yaWFsX0Jvb2ttYXJrcy0xODExMTE%3D&amp;utm_source=esp&amp;utm_medium=Email&amp;utm_campaign=Bookmarks&amp;CMP=bookmarks_email" rel="nofollow noopener">Join The Guardian's group read</a> if you have never read this tale before. It is an experience best shared with fellow Agathans.<br /><br />And I watched the <i>Marple</i> version again...AWFUL BAD TERRIBLE BAD STOOPUD BAD</span>

<div id="review_1829388913" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1829388913" />
    <a title="Mansuriah Hassan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26126450-mansuriah-hassan"><img alt="Mansuriah Hassan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580314850p2/26126450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1829388913?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mansuriah Hassan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mansuriah Hassan" href="/user/show/26126450-mansuriah-hassan">Mansuriah Hassan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26126450-mansuriah-hassan?shelf=agatha-christie">agatha-christie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1829388913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15260559543047273999">This is a chilling stand alone novel by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie' title='Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Agatha Christie</a>. <b>Endless Night</b> is quite different than Agatha Christie's Poirot or Marple series. The story is narrated by the main character, Micheal Rogers, a young man with grandeur ideas but with no obvious means of attaining it. He is fascinated with <i>Gipsy's Acre</i> - a plot of land in rural England that is said to be cursed by the Gypsies who once lived there and who were driven away.<br/><br/>While walking around the property that has come up for sale, he meets </span>
  <span id="freeText15260559543047273999" style="display:none">This is a chilling stand alone novel by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie</a>. <b>Endless Night</b> is quite different than Agatha Christie's Poirot or Marple series. The story is narrated by the main character, Micheal Rogers, a young man with grandeur ideas but with no obvious means of attaining it. He is fascinated with <i>Gipsy's Acre</i> - a plot of land in rural England that is said to be cursed by the Gypsies who once lived there and who were driven away.<br /><br />While walking around the property that has come up for sale, he meets an attractive young American woman, Ellie. A whirlwind of romance results in him marrying the very lovely and the rich heiress to a fabulous fortune. They hired an architect to build their dream house at <i>Gipsy's Acre</i>. But the land is cursed and soon a chain of tragedies struck the newlyweds like a very black cloud. .<br /><br />I quite enjoyed the inner monologue and the first person narration and about halfway through I was held in the grip of the most uneasy sense of creepiness that started colouring the story. There were points in the book where I actually looked over my shoulder. The suspense, character development and smattering of clues that only made sense as such at the end all make for a superb, edge of your seat portrayal of the inner workings of a mind gone horribly wrong.<br /><br />If you enjoy character development over plot happenings, glimpsing into a personality driven by darkness and a book that will have you thinking about it days after you've finished, then this is the novel for you. Most of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie</a>'s books can best be described as cracking thrillers. But <b>Endless Night</b> almost has the feel of a ghost story or a horror tale. <br /><br />A psychological thriller like I never expected..</span>
  <a data-text-id="15260559543047273999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3336296877" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3336296877" />
    <a title="jade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11030012-jade"><img alt="jade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562419355p2/11030012.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3336296877?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jade" href="/user/show/11030012-jade">jade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">murder mystery fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to jade by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/107881343-shannon">Shannon</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11030012-jade?shelf=murder-mysteries">murder-mysteries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3336296877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12786744562690812628"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‘look here,’ i said, ‘people like to collect disasters. that’s the way stories build themselves up about a place.’</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>another murder mystery standalone involving a love story and a possibly cursed property. buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/107881343-shannon' rel='nofollow noopener'>shannon</a> :)<br/><br/>there’s a couple of things in <i>endless night</i> that felt distinctly different from the usual in a agatha christie murder mystery. first up, the setting and imagery: it’s reminiscent of <b>gothic horror</b>, putting a strange but grand house at the forefront of the stor</span>
  <span id="freeText12786744562690812628" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‘look here,’ i said, ‘people like to collect disasters. that’s the way stories build themselves up about a place.’</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />another murder mystery standalone involving a love story and a possibly cursed property. buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/107881343-shannon" rel="nofollow noopener">shannon</a> :)<br /><br />there’s a couple of things in <i>endless night</i> that felt distinctly different from the usual in a agatha christie murder mystery. first up, the setting and imagery: it’s reminiscent of <b>gothic horror</b>, putting a strange but grand house at the forefront of the story; an architectural wonder dampened by an intense sense of foreboding.<br /><br />secondly, the characters: <b>mike</b>, our narrator, is a bit of a working class drifter, whose voice sounds appropriately cavalier and casual. he’s much more characterized than the usual standalone narrator in a christie novel; even more so thanks to the meandering style the story takes.<br /><br />he’s the perfectly rational guy for a spooky mystery, and we spend a lot of time getting to know him before we meet the love of his life: <b>ellie</b>. she’s a rich girl from america, who falls for this handsome stranger who’s enchanted by <i>her</i> rather than her money.<br /><br />it all seems like a straightforward love story in which mike and ellie deal with the aftermath of a <b>poor-guy-marries-rich-girl</b> conflict. various family members of ellie run to england to needle and judge mike, who feels like a fish out of water when confronted with ellie’s intricate business dealings. meanwhile, the sense of dread remains -- and it isn’t until relatively late in the story when Things Start Happening.<br /><br />if i had to label it as anything, i’d have to say that this is more of a <b>modern psychological thriller</b> with gothic elements than a usual cozy murder mystery. it’s an interesting angle to take, though i did like christie’s writing in this a bit less than usual; it feels overly <b>wordy</b> and repetitive, another complete opposite from what i usually expect from her.<br /><br />the reveal at the end -- because of course there is one -- is good, and very well-executed. <br /><br />however... coming off of having read many agatha christie books in a row, i can’t help but feel i’ve seen elements of this story before, albeit used or presented in a different way. considering the amount of decades her career spans, that’s not very strange -- and i think being your own best competition is a compliment in and of itself.<br /><br />also, a brief caveat of this book showing its age: the house that plays a big part in this is built upon a property called ‘g*psy acre’, which is apparently haunted. the book leans a lot into old and unfortunate stereotypes concerning the romani people, which was very grating.<br /><br /><b>bottom line:</b> entertaining, and i had a good time reading it. but it didn’t necessarily pop for me, and it’s not one that i’m liable to remember when someone asks me about my favorite christie stories.<br /><br />✎ <i>3.0 stars.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12786744562690812628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2123275664" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2123275664" />
    <a title="Jason Koivu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu"><img alt="Jason Koivu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560521450p2/1742824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2123275664?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2123275664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2605004893533463384">The last fifth of <i>Endless Night</i> was really good! The other fifths? Not so good.<br/><br/>This novel reads like a gothic romance horror soap opera...so, a little like the old Dark Shadows tv show. Only the gothic horror isn't particularly scary. Hell, it's not really even spooky. Soap Opera though? Yeah, I'm feeling that!<br/><br/>Here's the deal. This lacks the razor-sharp writing of Agatha Christie's earlier work, where a premium was placed on word economy. It meanders. For instance, the narrator is very chatty. D</span>
  <span id="freeText2605004893533463384" style="display:none">The last fifth of <i>Endless Night</i> was really good! The other fifths? Not so good.<br /><br />This novel reads like a gothic romance horror soap opera...so, a little like the old Dark Shadows tv show. Only the gothic horror isn't particularly scary. Hell, it's not really even spooky. Soap Opera though? Yeah, I'm feeling that!<br /><br />Here's the deal. This lacks the razor-sharp writing of Agatha Christie's earlier work, where a premium was placed on word economy. It meanders. For instance, the narrator is very chatty. Dialogues contain unnecessary exchanges. Sort of like...<br /><br />"A equals B."<br />"Oh really?"<br />"Yeah, really."<br />"Okay then."<br /> "So, as I was saying, A equals B."<br /><br />I wanted to say that Christie was looking to bend the old romance genre. You see, in her day, the dime store novel was all about the poor-girl-meets-rich-guy love story. It feels like <i>Endless Night</i> is trying to turn that on its head. That would be great! And perhaps that was the intent, but the publication date puts this past the point where this idea would've been cutting edge.<br /><br />My other theory was that Christie was trying to get with the times and create more meaningful characterization. Let's face it, some of her early mysteries are almost entirely plot-driven and have little room for character development. <i>Endless Night</i> certainly spends a lot of time in the mind of the narrator. However, I'm not sold that this was her intent. <br /><br />I suppose what it comes down to is, <i>Endless Night</i> is Christie's attempt at a psychological thriller and it didn't quite work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2605004893533463384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1047715011" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1047715011" />
    <a title="Vanessa J." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j"><img alt="Vanessa J." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468102148p2/19590155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1047715011?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa J." href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j">Vanessa J.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=agatha-christie">agatha-christie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1047715011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14653436924762523158"><blockquote>
  <i>Every morn and every night,<br/>Some are born to sweet delight.<br/>Every morn and every night,<br/>Some are born to endless night.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>When people mention Agatha Christie to me, I always think about a woman writing murder mysteries. You know those: Someone is killed and another someone wants to figure out who's the responsible for that death. Getting into gothic passages, though, is not something I imagined her to do.<br/><br/>More than 60% of this book consists on getting to know our narrator Michael - Mike - Rogers. H</span>
  <span id="freeText14653436924762523158" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Every morn and every night,<br>Some are born to sweet delight.<br>Every morn and every night,<br>Some are born to endless night.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>When people mention Agatha Christie to me, I always think about a woman writing murder mysteries. You know those: Someone is killed and another someone wants to figure out who's the responsible for that death. Getting into gothic passages, though, is not something I imagined her to do.<br><br>More than 60% of this book consists on getting to know our narrator Michael - Mike - Rogers. He's a man who would - let's say, now that I'm rereading Harry Potter - belong to Slytherin: He's cunning and with an ambition greater than a whale.<br><br>People have always thought he's a man who will never settle down, marry a girl and build his own life. That's when he meets Ellie, decides to marry her in secret, and starts his life in Gipsy's Acre, a place the villagers are afraid of because of urban legends that say it's cursed.<br><br>But of course, our charming protagonist does not believe in the legends, and too late does he realise the warnings people gave to his wife were real.<br><br>I'm completely aware I'm kind of spoiling more than half the book, but you really have to trust me when I say the very important parts of the book happen after 75% of it. That's when Agatha Christie fooled me. She fooled me again like an idiot.<br><br>Nothing could have prevented me for falling into her trap. I guess the only piece of advice I could give you without ruining the book is: Don't believe everything your senses tell you, and when I say "senses" I mean eyes, ears, nose, hands and everything. <b>You are only to be deceived if you trust them.</b><br><br>That said, I have to praise Christie for being able to make me like a character I would usually hate. You see, Mike is <i>very</i> charming. I loved him ever since he started to tell the story. Oh, but that's not what would have made me hate him. What I didn't like was that he's the kind of person who likes to get things the easy, lazy way. That's something I really despise. Yet I loved being inside his head.<br><br>I also loved the way she portrayed the rest of the characters - all through Mike's thoughts and feelings. She made my mind give a complete twist, making me hate certain characters I probably should have paid more attention to, and making me be suspicious of others who weren't even important part in the plot (or so I thought).<br><br>That's just the way it was with the other work I've read by her, in which I was fooled too, though I didn't feel as stupid as I did when I reached the end of the book.<br><br>Perhaps the sign that says a mystery book is good (because there is in fact a mystery around 70%) is how much of an imbecile you feel. The more idiotic you feel, the better the book is, and in this case, I can say I am like:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453135856i/17785690.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Which is to say, I wholehertedly recommend this book. Now leave me alone because I still feel terribly ashamed of myself. Gah! I bet Christie would be laughing! How she has mocked me...<br><br>P.S.: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Damned unreliable narrators. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14653436924762523158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13128328884858072453"><i>"I’d no real idea that that wasn’t all there was to it. I suppose it happens to everyone sooner or later and it happens suddenly. You don’t think as you imagine you’re going to think: ‘This might be the girl for me… This is the girl who is going to be mine.’ At least, I didn’t feel it that way.   <span id="freeText13128328884858072453" style="display:none"><i>"I’d no real idea that that wasn’t all there was to it. I suppose it happens to everyone sooner or later and it happens suddenly. You don’t think as you imagine you’re going to think: ‘This might be the girl for me… This is the girl who is going to be mine.’ At least, I didn’t feel it that way. I didn’t know that when it happened it would happen quite suddenly. That I would say: ‘That’s the girl I belong to. I’m hers. I belong to her, utterly, for always.’ No. I never dreamed it would be like that. Didn’t one of the old comedians say once– wasn’t it one of his stock jokes? ‘I’ve been in love once and if I felt it coming on again I tell you I’d emigrate.’ It was the same with me. If I had known, if I had only known what it could all come to mean I’d have emigrated too! If I’d been wise, that is."</i><br /> <br />Endless Night is one of Dame Agatha's lesser known novels. However, it is easily one of her best. <br /> <br />The narrator describes this story as a love story but it is clear from the outset - and obviously knowing that it is an AC story - that not all is well and that there are powers conspiring against the main characters. It is for the reader to follow the narrator into the story of Gipsy's Acre, his story. <br /> <br />I'm not going to give anything away here but just want to say that this book had me hooked and led me down the garden path right until the very end. And for someone who is quick to describe Dame Agatha's mysteries as formulaic, this is not easy to admit. Well, ok, it is. I enjoyed every minute of being mislead by this story.<br /> <br /><i>"In my end is my beginning…That’s a quotation I’ve often heard people say. It sounds all right– but what does it really mean? Is there ever any particular spot where one can put one’s finger and say: ‘It all began that day, at such a time and such a place, with such an incident?’ "</i></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer60513693910100568">Per usual, I really enjoyed Christie’s beautiful writing style.   <span id="freeText60513693910100568" style="display:none">Per usual, I really enjoyed Christie’s beautiful writing style. My one ‘complaint’ with the story is that unfortunately, I guessed who did it right off that bat. It was almost a little too obvious where I was hoping for some other twist to really catch me by surprise, but unfortunately this was not the case. That being said, I’ve been finding this problem with many of her books in that they contain a lot of tropes that though I’m sure she was one of the first to start them, they are now overly done and easy to spot. Again, this is no fault of hers and I nonetheless did enjoy it overall!<br /><br />Find me on Booktube! <a href="http://www.youtube.com/c/rusticpages" rel="nofollow noopener">youtube.com/c/rusticpages</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5542855-amy-waitforit?shelf=murder">murder</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5542855-amy-waitforit?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer295843020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10569561518860265691"><b>2.5 stars - A Strange tale</b><br/><br/>I want to start by saying I <i>love</i> Agatha Christie, I have read pretty much all of her books and Poirot is on my list of fictional characters I would love to have dinner with.<br/><br/><b>But</b> <br/><br/>I have to say that I really did not enjoy this story nearly as much as I hoped I would. The story is told by Michael, a young man with little money and big expectations who marries Ellie (an innocent young rich girl). The story surrounds 'Gipsy Acre', a large house and plot of land in the English</span>
  <span id="freeText10569561518860265691" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars - A Strange tale</b><br /><br />I want to start by saying I <i>love</i> Agatha Christie, I have read pretty much all of her books and Poirot is on my list of fictional characters I would love to have dinner with.<br /><br /><b>But</b> <br /><br />I have to say that I really did not enjoy this story nearly as much as I hoped I would. The story is told by Michael, a young man with little money and big expectations who marries Ellie (an innocent young rich girl). The story surrounds 'Gipsy Acre', a large house and plot of land in the English countryside which is supposedly under a Gypsy curse. Well of course this young married couple buy the land and build their dream house. <br />So why was I disappointed? Well the story was slow, the actual crime doesn't take place until page 163 of a 224 Page book (I was so shocked I actually took a mental note of the page number). The majority of the book is the courtship of Michael and Ellie and their family matters with the occasional crazy gypsy lady appearing to warn them of the curse and to tell Ellie that she predicted bad things. I have to say by about page 140 I was pretty much begging the gypsy lady (or anybody really) to <b>DO</b> something, but I persevered as I know that Agatha Christie is famous for her twists and turns. Finally as I say a crime is finally committed and the rest of the book is actually pretty good. It is written with Christie's usual level of suspense and wrong turns so it gives plenty of opportunity for guessing and thinking.<br /><br />I have to say that although I didn't like the story much, I loved the writing. The imagery was brilliant, and I could envision the setting perfectly. The characters were well written and their characters were easily definable (although you do have 163 pages to sort this out).<br /><br />As I said before I love Agatha Christie's work and will not let this little disappointment stop me from reading more of her books. I just wish that this story had a little more opportunity for thinking, I do like to exercise 'The little grey cells'.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10569561518860265691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12125027294737442074">One of Agatha Christie's later mysteries (published in 1967), <i>Endless Night</i> is also one of her best. The twist at the end is brilliant. I have read it three times. The first time I read it, at least 12 years ago, she really fooled me, though when I reread it much later, I could see that the clues are all there if you can put them together right. This time I listened to the audiobook, with Hugh Fraser's excellent narration.<br/></span>

<div id="review_245288677" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/245288677" />
    <a title="F.R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1309606-f-r"><img alt="F.R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544886612p2/1309606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/245288677?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="F.R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="F.R." href="/user/show/1309606-f-r">F.R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer245288677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14556290132150030716">Well, this is an interesting little oddity. If I’d picked this novel up blind, not knowing who the author was, then I think I could have got through the first few chapters without being able to guess. Here is a narrator who is just so un-Christie. For a start he’s very much working class, your callow and unpolished drifter. A good looking and smooth-talking boy, who at points seemed to me like he’d strayed in from a Joe Orton play. The tone is very un-Christie too, and Michael Roberts – the narr</span>
  <span id="freeText14556290132150030716" style="display:none">Well, this is an interesting little oddity. If I’d picked this novel up blind, not knowing who the author was, then I think I could have got through the first few chapters without being able to guess. Here is a narrator who is just so un-Christie. For a start he’s very much working class, your callow and unpolished drifter. A good looking and smooth-talking boy, who at points seemed to me like he’d strayed in from a Joe Orton play. The tone is very un-Christie too, and Michael Roberts – the narrator in question – reminded me of some of Jim Thompson’s more gauche protagonists. (Dusty Rhodes in ‘A Swell Looking Babe’ came to mind.) This is a not very bright lad who thinks he’s smart at points, but doesn’t have as keen a grip on the world as he believes he does.<br /><br />Michael Roberts – a sometimes chauffer, waiter and bouncer – meets a young American heiress, one of the richest women in the world, and the two fall in love. After an elopement, they move into a house which has a gypsies’ curse upon it and there tragedy strikes. It’s a well set-up and delivered tale, although the ending – which I didn’t guess until I was almost upon it – does feel a tad too rushed and unconvincing.<br /><br />Part of me is quite fascinated by Dame Agatha’s oeuvre, as I find her work hypnotically compulsive even as the flaws scream out at me. But here, those flaws aren’t as much in evidence (although when the dialogue begins, my of my, you can really tell that Christie is the author). Without a doubt – of the ones I’ve read – this is the best and certainly the most intriguing of her books. <br /><br /><br /><i>(I’ve just seen on Wikipedia that Miss Marple will be crow-barred into this tale for the next TV Series – much as they did for ‘The Pale Horse’. Now that just seems a way to take something that’s genuinely interesting and make is as bland as cabbage soup. Sigh.)</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14556290132150030716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Just not to my liking. And it seems to m</span>
  <span id="freeText1169144162332186375" style="display:none">This is not my favorite Christie book, although it does have my favorite twist. Still, it wasn't my style.<br /><br />There is a twist that I can't tell you about because I will reveal the clou of the whole book (but maybe I'll write something in spoilers below) that I absolutely love. And this very twist has appeared in this book. Unfortunately for me, it was way too late, and by that time I had completely lost interest in this story.<br /><br />This is by no means a bad story. Just not to my liking. And it seems to me that I also have a period now when I am much more strict in judging my books and much more fussy. I have no patience for books that don't interest me in the first few chapters, or books that have threads that I don't like. And this book has just become a victim.<br /><br />I generally like fast paced books. I also like when a book starts strongly (with an earthquake as Hitchcock would say), I like when a corpse appears in the first pages and an investigation begins immediately. This is not a story of this type. This one has a rather slow pace and slowly builds up tension and atmosphere. Efficient and skillful, but I'm afraid too slowly for my current mood. Nor is this a book written in one of Agatha Christie's well-known patterns. This is not a locked room murder or whodunit mystery, most of the time it is not a murder mystery at all. And that's what I was counting on.<br /><br />ATTENTION, VERY BIG SPOILER (revealing the end of the book)<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />I love it when the main character turns out to be a murderer. It will not be an exaggeration to say that this is one of my absolutely beloved twists. But I like it even more when the murderer then manages to evade justice. I think it requires exceptional writing skills from the author. Create a complex and at the same time probable plot that will lead to the protagonist escaping punishment. Unfortunately, this happens very rarely. And I'm always a bit disappointed when the main character gets caught. This was also the case this time.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It was definitely not what I wanted and generally not to my liking. But it's a good story, and other readers will probably like it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1169144162332186375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer907378065" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1038057004849611840">This is a stand -alone novel by Agatha Christie and is one that I had not read before. I have to admit that Christie is undoubtedly my favourite author of all time and, whether re-visiting favourite characters such as Poirot, or coming to one of her books for the first time, it always feels as though you are reading something familiar. In fact, immersing yourself in a Christie novel is rather like slipping into a warm pool and being taken effortlessly on a journey – she is the most capable plott</span>
  <span id="freeText1038057004849611840" style="display:none">This is a stand -alone novel by Agatha Christie and is one that I had not read before. I have to admit that Christie is undoubtedly my favourite author of all time and, whether re-visiting favourite characters such as Poirot, or coming to one of her books for the first time, it always feels as though you are reading something familiar. In fact, immersing yourself in a Christie novel is rather like slipping into a warm pool and being taken effortlessly on a journey – she is the most capable plotter and absolutely joyous to read.<br /><br />In this book we meet Michael Rogers; a rather shiftless young man, whose aimless lifestyle is about to change when he comes across the beautiful young Ellie outside a ruined house called ‘The Towers’, but known to local as Gipsy’s Acre. Michael had the area in mind for the house of his dreams, but does not have the means to build or buy it. However, Ellie turns out to a wealthy heiress and, before long they have married secretly with the help of Ellie’s companion Greta. Soon, Ellie has commissioned the building of their dream house on Gipsy’s Acre – even though both Michael and Ellie have been warned off by old Mrs Lee, who insists that the land has been cursed by gypsies, who were turned off the land. <br /><br />From the beginning, you feel that something terrible will happen and this is a dark novel, with many plot twists and turns and a surprising ending. I am delighted that I finally got around to reading it and that, as always, Agatha Christie did not disappoint.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1038057004849611840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_151164289" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151164289" />
    <a title="Laurel Young" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3137295-laurel-young"><img alt="Laurel Young" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500435810p2/3137295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151164289?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurel Young" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurel Young" href="/user/show/3137295-laurel-young">Laurel Young</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3137295-laurel-young?shelf=my-year-of-agatha">my-year-of-agatha</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151164289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer208153691779967951">Had I never read Agatha Christie's other works, I might well be giving Endless Night 5 stars--genuinely creepy atmosphere, a challenging narrative voice for her to carry off (that of a young working-class man), and a breathtaking twist at the end...what's not to love? Well, in my case, the trouble is that she's done the best elements of this novel before, and done them better earlier in her long career. She's taken one of her all-time most brilliant and shocking ideas from The Murder of Roger Ac</span>
  <span id="freeText208153691779967951" style="display:none">Had I never read Agatha Christie's other works, I might well be giving Endless Night 5 stars--genuinely creepy atmosphere, a challenging narrative voice for her to carry off (that of a young working-class man), and a breathtaking twist at the end...what's not to love? Well, in my case, the trouble is that she's done the best elements of this novel before, and done them better earlier in her long career. She's taken one of her all-time most brilliant and shocking ideas from The Murder of Roger Ackroyd, added elements from her Miss Marple story "The Case of the Caretaker", mixed them together with Henry James' The Wings of the Dove...and it all adds up to Endless Night. <br /><br />I know that Dame Agatha could not have expected her readers in 1967 to have a novel she wrote 40 years earlier AND one of her lesser-known short stories clearly in mind while reading Endless Night. She liked to take an idea and try it from different angles, and certainly she does a fine job of building suspense here. It's just that some ideas are too iconic to ever re-use, and she was her own toughest competition. 1967 Agatha Christie just cannot compete with 1926 Agatha Christie for ingenuity, although she could best any other mystery writer before or since! So although this novel is actually quite strong when taken by itself, I cannot help but see it as derivative.</span>
  <a data-text-id="208153691779967951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6384026583213231705" style="display:none">What did I just finish...wow❤️<br />.<br />I won't write a huge review because I feel if I try to tell even about a small plot it would become a spoiler and I don't wanna give spoilers.<br />.<br />This is quite different from other Agatha Christie books and I like that. <div id="review_3419088446" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3419088446" />
    <a title="Helio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73548608-helio"><img alt="Helio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577746336p2/73548608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3419088446?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helio" href="/user/show/73548608-helio">Helio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3419088446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13496764864059716809">I knew this story was not going to have a happy ending. It had miserable wooden characters in an intriguing situation: poor man marries rich woman to live on cursed land. The man was a scoundrel and the author did little to persuade the reader why the woman fell for him. The first two thirds dragged like a painter haphazardly slapping paint on a canvas. The story became interesting in the last third as a fuzzy picture came to emerge of what had been going on. The characters were unlikeable; the </span>
  <span id="freeText13496764864059716809" style="display:none">I knew this story was not going to have a happy ending. It had miserable wooden characters in an intriguing situation: poor man marries rich woman to live on cursed land. The man was a scoundrel and the author did little to persuade the reader why the woman fell for him. The first two thirds dragged like a painter haphazardly slapping paint on a canvas. The story became interesting in the last third as a fuzzy picture came to emerge of what had been going on. The characters were unlikeable; the plot preposterous. 2.5 marked down to a 2.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13496764864059716809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_901695873" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/901695873" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6316008-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600893038p2/6316008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/901695873?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/6316008-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6316008-chris?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6316008-chris?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6316008-chris?shelf=2014-favorites">2014-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer901695873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11329988618388981702">Brilliant. Absolutely brilliant. <br/><br/>A stand alone novel that is more psychological study than mystery. This is one of Agatha Christie's favorites and I can see why. What starts out as a sort of analysis of class dynamics and the psychology of privilege turns into a very chilling exploration of madness.<br/><br/>5 stars.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SY8TIrLKDvqIvpue7IIGpo3HKoeTEKUTHcpAOy/MsyTDgn3Lw/JivZgx5xuKUL2Rg2Vux8ZWq2cpG4IDif45Rg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('00wLKNDsDlnI9rn30yeLAbzp1YqCjf2/a6DiaUTKTSpZQWXBodRiHth5xXK19TA2skuRytfL88tfcSBR4vjHSA==')})
  }
//]]>

He cannot convince Sylvia Rule of his innocence, however, and she marches away in a rage.\n\nShaken, Poirot goes inside, only to find that he has a visitor waiting for him -- a man called John McCrodden who also claims also to have received a letter from Poirot that morning, accusing him of the murder of Barnabas Pandy...\n\nPoirot wonders how many more letters of this sort have been sent in his name.
